    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2195786443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2195786443" />
    <a title="Candace Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33995641-candace-robinson"><img alt="Candace Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530157383p2/33995641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2195786443?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace Robinson" href="/user/show/33995641-candace-robinson">Candace Robinson</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2195786443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5549725972096376590">Do-do-do-do-do ... so I fought back and forth with this book the whole read. I was bored a lot during the first 40%, then things got interesting, then I got bored again, then things were magnanimous. But, Frost Demon, you make every scene you are in worth reading. I seriously think I would have enjoyed it more if he had his own POV. Like we get POVs from a lot of others, but never my boy! Whyyyyyyyy nottttttttt??????????<br/><br/>At times my issues came with Vasya. I felt sometimes she needed more emotion</span>
  <span id="freeText5549725972096376590" style="display:none">Do-do-do-do-do ... so I fought back and forth with this book the whole read. I was bored a lot during the first 40%, then things got interesting, then I got bored again, then things were magnanimous. But, Frost Demon, you make every scene you are in worth reading. I seriously think I would have enjoyed it more if he had his own POV. Like we get POVs from a lot of others, but never my boy! Whyyyyyyyy nottttttttt??????????<br /><br />At times my issues came with Vasya. I felt sometimes she needed more emotions? I guess? Sometimes, or a lot of the time, I can be a robotic person so I do get that. Also, when it came to Morozko, I would have preferred more of a team effort when it came to certain things. A lot of the time these days, as I've said before, authors are making the girls so bad ass and then the guy seems like a pathetic weakling. I want a team effort—equality—not the guy saying, "let's go hide in a corner," and then the girl is all like, "I'm going to go win this war!" I don't get it... Yet there were some perfect scenes between Vasya and Morozko that were so good and swoooooooon! <br /><br />When it came to the Winter of the Witch, not sure if the right word is political or if the book felt like it had more of an agenda, but when it came to that stuff, I was just like come on already! I want more of the magical feel I first felt! But don't worry, there are some gorgeous scenes, too.<br /><br />Anyway, the book was beautifully written. I just miss the whimsical/fairy tale feel of the first book and the intriguing feeling I had while reading the second book. Also Konstantin, the creep, is still crazy! His character is so interesting at times, but I also want to smack him for his insane thoughts. I will say that the Bear is probably one of my new favorite characters—ever. And Sasha I still love more than anything. Overall I did like the way it came to an end, but can a certain character get their own book now???</span>
  <a data-text-id="5549725972096376590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2616153101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2616153101" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2616153101?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616153101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6511786846914569925">Katherine Arden completes the wonder that is the stellar Winternight trilogy, and leaves me in pieces, distraught with a deep sense of loss that this is the end. This is epic storytelling as it begins with the ashes of Moskva and a traumatised people susceptible to the charismatic priest Konstantin, a man overcome by a maelstrom of feelings, with fear of Vasya dominating. Branded a witch and pariah, Vasya is to be tested beyond human endurance, acquiring a fire within, wracked with grief and los</span>
  <span id="freeText6511786846914569925" style="display:none">Katherine Arden completes the wonder that is the stellar Winternight trilogy, and leaves me in pieces, distraught with a deep sense of loss that this is the end. This is epic storytelling as it begins with the ashes of Moskva and a traumatised people susceptible to the charismatic priest Konstantin, a man overcome by a maelstrom of feelings, with fear of Vasya dominating. Branded a witch and pariah, Vasya is to be tested beyond human endurance, acquiring a fire within, wracked with grief and loss. Immersed in magic within the vast enchanted lands of Midnight, she travels exhausted and broken, becoming aware of her family history and legacy, making her the heir to her unforgiving great grandmother, but Vasya has much to learn. The winter king, the death god Morozko, has sacrificed himself for Vasya, but at a terrible price as the spirit of chaos, the bear, is unleashed on a Moscow already on its knees, as the diminished power of the chyerti leaves its open to the further incoming bloodlust, death and destruction.<br /><br />The Grand Prince of Moskva, Dmitrii, Vasya's cousin is beseiged by dangers from all sides, the rising power of Konstantin, now discarding all remnants of his Christian faith for a devil's bargain with the bear in return for power. The Tatars with vast forces of fighting men, under the leadership of Mamai, seek silver from Dmitrii, with plans to decimate and conquer Rus through war, if the silver is unforthcoming. Terrified for her family and Rus, Vasya seeks Morozko, unprepared for what she finds. In this dark fairytale, Vasya comes of age, becomes a woman, becoming aware of her abilities, exercising her magic and rallying to become the third force of power as many chyerti, and Pozhar, the firebird, form an alliance with her. Magic, however, is a gift and a curse, rich in its temptations, but exposing her to an all consuming madness that threatens all that ties her to her family, Rus, humanity, and love. To fight the forces that threaten Rus and her family, Vasya ventures into unthinkable terrritory, making common cause with the spirit of chaos, revealing they share more more than she has forseen. Only unity can offer the miniscule hope of winning the David and Goliath battles that loom, offering a future for co-existence between Christian, Pagan and the Grand Prince, and the foundation for an independent Rus. <br /><br />War rallies disparate parties but inevitably horror, loss and grief are its repercussions, and nothing Vasya can do can prevent the gravest of loss as her grief overflows. The waters of death and the waters of life offer some much needed amelioration as a close spirit joyfully returns. Katherine Arden has taken the framework of actual Russian history, and weaves a spellbinding tale of Vasya, a young woman unwilling to accept convention on the role of women, challenging the path of either marriage or the convent, the only options available. Arden's storytelling is atmospheric, vital, vibrant and unforgettable. It is outstanding, feminist, conjoining the mortal with the immortal, and located in the rich mythology and legends of Russian folklore. I don't know what Arden will do next, but I guarantee whatever it is, I will be reading it without fail. What can I say?? Just read this. Many thanks to Random House Ebury for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6511786846914569925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2219280871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2219280871" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2219280871?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=bookriot-read-harder-challenge-2020">bookriot-read-harder-challenge-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219280871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17713634853696752705"><b>fulfilling my 2020 goal to read (at least) one book each month that i bought in hardcover and put off reading long enough that it is now in paperback.<br/><br/>AND CONVENIENTLY *ALSO*<br/><br/>fulfilling book riot's 2020 read harder challenge task #9: Read the LAST book in a series.</b><br/>********************************<br/>an absolutely perfect ending to a trilogy i have loved every step of the way. <br/><br/>richly detailed and emotionally satisfying, everything that happens here slots perfectly into the world arden has created and r</span>
  <span id="freeText17713634853696752705" style="display:none"><b>fulfilling my 2020 goal to read (at least) one book each month that i bought in hardcover and put off reading long enough that it is now in paperback.<br><br>AND CONVENIENTLY *ALSO*<br><br>fulfilling book riot's 2020 read harder challenge task #9: Read the LAST book in a series.</b><br>********************************<br>an absolutely perfect ending to a trilogy i have loved every step of the way. <br><br>richly detailed and emotionally satisfying, everything that happens here slots perfectly into the world arden has created and respects the events of her previous books—every grief and failure, every bittersweet success is 100% <i>earned</i>. one of my personal grumbles with fantasy as a genre is that, where there is magic, where there are characters with <i>powers</i>, obstacles are frequently too easily overcome and all the potential for delicious dramatic tension is sidestepped. here, nothing is easy, nothing is deus ex machina'd away, and when powerful beings do intervene, it is never without a cost. <br><br>oh, and although it was telegraphed pretty clearly in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917.The_Girl_in_the_Tower__Winternight_Trilogy___2_" title="The Girl in the Tower (Winternight Trilogy, #2) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Tower</a>, allow me to bellow <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[SOLOVEY!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>vasya as a character is just *finger kiss* <i>mwah</i>. such depth and authentically written growth and maturity; everything she's overcome has left its mark on her, and she grows into her womanself and her witchself beautifully, but not without considerable struggle and loss. her bravery and strength and defiance, her willingness to sacrifice herself on her own terms but not as someone else's pawn, her abiding love for her people even as they turn against her—these are pretty common qualities of the hero archetype, but arden breathes fresh life into old tropes and the result is a heroine who is both likable and fallible, shining up outta those pages, dusting herself off from each struggle with new scars and renewed determination. <br><br>it is gorgeous. all of it. <br><br>it's historical fantasy in setting and atmosphere—russian folklore woven into actual historical conflicts, incorporating a more modern feminist sensibility without shifting it too far into the trend of MAGICAL GIRL CAN DO ALL THE THINGS EFFORTLESSLY!<br><br>i don't want to get into too many details, because it's book 3 of a thing, but i need to shout-out that l'il mushroom ded grib as my favorite new character. i'm sure this series will be turned into a show or film at some point, and i'm gonna want some ded grib merch. to play with my baby yoda merch. because i am grown.<br><br>also, as much as i'm immune to romance in my entertainments<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581434916ra/28944652.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>vasya and morozko's relationship arc is pretty great. not only do i love me some cold hands, but i appreciate that theirs is a qualified romance, with limits that are addressed in a way that few books involving entanglements between immortals and mortals bother to do. <i>"As I could, I loved you"</i> is my <i>"You complete me"</i> and like everything else in this series, all of their pleasure is mingled with pain.<br><br>anyway, there's your zero-plot review of a book i five-starred. i loved this trilogy, and i know i will love whatever she writes next.<br><br>************************************<br><br>SO CLOSE TO MY BIRTHDAY? HOW KIND YOU ARE!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2603857792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2603857792" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2603857792?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2603857792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3186024161009269462">"There is nothing but power in this world. People are divided into those who have it and those who have it not. Which will you be....."<br/><br/>There is a lot of power in the final book of the Winternight Trilogy. This book starts off where <i>The Girl in the Tower</i> ends. If you have not read the first two books in the series, it is imperative that you read them first otherwise you will not know what is going on in this book. <br/><br/>I am not even going to attempt to give a synopsis of the book. There is just so muc</span>
  <span id="freeText3186024161009269462" style="display:none">"There is nothing but power in this world. People are divided into those who have it and those who have it not. Which will you be....."<br /><br />There is a lot of power in the final book of the Winternight Trilogy. This book starts off where <i>The Girl in the Tower</i> ends. If you have not read the first two books in the series, it is imperative that you read them first otherwise you will not know what is going on in this book. <br /><br />I am not even going to attempt to give a synopsis of the book. There is just so much going on, but I will say that I appreciate how Arden has one book flow into the next. I also love that these books are based on Russian fairy-tales/folklore and history. I am not a big fan of fantasy, but this series worked for me. Although, <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i> was my favorite, this one served as a very nice conclusion. It is darker, there is more danger, lives are lost (some are just gut wrenching), battles are fought and won, there is romance (finally!), and Vasya really comes into her own (and her power). Plus, we get re-acquainted with favorite characters from the series (Solovey and Morozko for me), plus there are villains. I will admit, even though he is a villain, I couldn't help but like and snicker at the Bear a.k.a Medved. Then there are the new characters and realms/worlds, such as Midnight, which was a nice addition to the story and serves to give Vasya more knowledge about her family. <br /><br />"There are no monsters in the world, and no saints. Only infinite shades woven into the same tapestry, light and dark. One man's monster is another man's beloved. The wise know that."<br /><br />There is a lot going on in this book and at times, the action felt drawn out. At times, I wanted it to move a little faster. A plus, in this book, is the vivid descriptions. We are dealing with a real place (Russia) but also with another world, magic, magical creatures, etc. so it helped tremendously that Arden gave the reader detailed descriptions. I found it was easy to visualize the book as I read. <br /><br />I believe most fans of this series will like how the trilogy ends. I like that Vasya made her own decisions and stood by them. She remained a strong female character throughout the series and ended strong. <br /><br />3.5 stars rounded up <br /><br />Thank you to Random House Publishing - Ballantine and NetGalley who provided me with a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. The thoughts and opinions expressed in this review are my own.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3186024161009269462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3221802493?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>

<div id="review_2205787237" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2205787237" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475256742p2/41788446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2205787237?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38391059-the-winter-of-the-witch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2205787237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11129060222292321799">I adored this beyond measure.<br/><br/>I am a huge fan of this trilogy, have been ever since reading the very first chapter of the first book. I was both super excited and a bit apprehensive before reading this book – but I didn’t have to worry because Katherine Arden absolutely sticks the landing here. This book is both a great conclusion to this brilliant series as well as a great book in its own right.<br/><br/>What Arden does better than most authors I read is building an atmosphere so immersive I become lost i</span>
  <span id="freeText11129060222292321799" style="display:none">I adored this beyond measure.<br /><br />I am a huge fan of this trilogy, have been ever since reading the very first chapter of the first book. I was both super excited and a bit apprehensive before reading this book – but I didn’t have to worry because Katherine Arden absolutely sticks the landing here. This book is both a great conclusion to this brilliant series as well as a great book in its own right.<br /><br />What Arden does better than most authors I read is building an atmosphere so immersive I become lost in her (impeccably researched) world. I found reading this book a very rewarding experience and I am definitely a life-long fan. Drawing on Russian fairy tales and real world figures to build a world uniquely her own, Arden tells a story of a girl and her choices. Whatever happens in this book is always filtered through Vasya’s lenses and her destiny and I am in love with this. Vasya is a difficult character but someone I could not help root for. I wanted her to find her place and be happy. She is allowed to be prickly and nurturing, she can be rash and caring, and altogether wonderfully rounded. Her relationship to the Winter King just worked for me in this book (I was not fully on board in the book before) and I really liked the overwhelming tenderness between those two.<br /><br />I adore how the world becomes more complicated as Vasya grows and the scope increases. Things that seemed very black and white to her in the first book become more ambivalent, people grow while staying true to their characterization, and overall the world becomes ever more believable.<br /><br />Arden has a very distinct and very beautiful writing style that hints at her influences while being very much her own thing and from the very first chapter I was glad to be back in her capable hands. There is a rhythm to her writing that I find very beautiful and this coupled with a story that wraps up strong makes this a strong contender for my favourite book of this year (I just know it’ll make the list).<br /><br />I received an ARC of this book courtesy of NetGalley and Ebury Publishing in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />You can find this review and other thoughts on books on <a href="https://ihavethoughtsonbooks.wordpress.com/2019/01/09/review-the-winter-of-the-witch-winternight-trilogy-3-by-katherine-arden/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11129060222292321799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2343174654" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343174654" />
    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343174654?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785039713" href="/book/show/38204046-the-winter-of-the-witch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343174654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16507831525829614283">5*****<br/><br/><i>”I have plucked snowdrops at Midwinter, died at my own choosing, and wept for a nightingale. Now I am beyond prophecy.”</i><br/><br/>Enchanting ! <br/>More action packed than the other two books but still maintains all of its magical elements and folklore. This book picks up straight after book 2 so we get to learn what happens of Vasya, Morozko, The Bear, Vasya’s family and Father Constantine, as well as many others. This book introduces us to more magical folklore, see Vasya use her magical skills, we get </span>
  <span id="freeText16507831525829614283" style="display:none">5*****<br /><br /><i>”I have plucked snowdrops at Midwinter, died at my own choosing, and wept for a nightingale. Now I am beyond prophecy.”</i><br /><br />Enchanting ! <br />More action packed than the other two books but still maintains all of its magical elements and folklore. This book picks up straight after book 2 so we get to learn what happens of Vasya, Morozko, The Bear, Vasya’s family and Father Constantine, as well as many others. This book introduces us to more magical folklore, see Vasya use her magical skills, we get to travel to enchanted places through Midnight and meet Baba Yaga. <br /><br />I love Vasya as a character and she will forever be one of my most favourite and most impactful heroines I have ever come across in literature. I would love to be like her- she’s a very inspirational female character to follow. She is absolutely smart, fierce, independent, devoted, passionate and brave. She wants a life of magic instead of traditional gender roles that others are trying to box her in to. We also get to see more Vasya and Morozko and see how their interactions develop. <br /><br />I purely enjoyed this final instalment and it was a fantastic way of finishing the series. (I am now just forever going to reread over them as they were so good!). <br /><br />I am obsessed with the winternight trilogy and now that I’ve finished it I am at a loss as to what to do - I’m very sad that it is over, but it is one of the best series I have ever read. Katherine Arden has made me fall in love with the world she created and the characters she shared with us.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3362934121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3362934121" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3362934121?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/42082394-the-winter-of-the-witch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=libby-app">libby-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=witchy-woman">witchy-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=magic-stuff">magic-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3362934121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer30846295790357040">I really thought this was the best of the bunch.<br/>The pacing was far better in <b>The Winter of the Witch</b> than it was in the first 2 books. Which to me, means the story itself wandered <i>less</i> and moved toward the action and resolution in a timely manner.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590752438ra/29560231.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Also, if you love horses, you'll love these books.<br/>I'm going to have to say I've never really seen the appeal of horses. When I was a kid I used to go help my neighbor lady take care of her horses in the summer. I wasn't a huge fan. They were nice horses</span>
  <span id="freeText30846295790357040" style="display:none">I really thought this was the best of the bunch.<br>The pacing was far better in <b>The Winter of the Witch</b> than it was in the first 2 books. Which to me, means the story itself wandered <i>less</i> and moved toward the action and resolution in a timely manner.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590752438ra/29560231.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, if you love horses, you'll love these books.<br>I'm going to have to say I've never really seen the appeal of horses. When I was a kid I used to go help my neighbor lady take care of her horses in the summer. I wasn't a huge fan. They were nice horses and all, and it wasn't like I had a bad experience, but they're such a pain in the ass as far as upkeep goes.<br>Cats. I like cats. Not a very needy pet, you know?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590938336ra/29571853.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>However, Vasya loves horses, talks to the horses, and her best friend is a horse.<br>Point is, horse lovers will really dig this book.<br>But that's neither here nor there because Vasya is about to get her ass burnt up by that shitty priest and his idiotic peasant followers. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590941027ra/29572541.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Unfortunately for the villagers, Vasya doesn't go up in flames. Instead, she pops out of the fire and eats all their babies!<br>No. Just kidding. But that would have been fun, also.<br>Instead, Morozko makes a deal with his brother to save her. Not sure she really needed him, but it's the thought that counts, you know?<br>Turns out, there's an army heading toward Moscow and it's up to Vasya to unite the humans and the otherworldy creatures to save her beloved Russia.<br>Now, if I were her, I would have left those assholes to their fate. &lt;--which is probably why this story isn't about <i>me</i>.<br>Anyway, it's summertime in Russia...<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590941027ra/29572542.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So, the Winter King, her biggest ally and the guy she loves, can't do anything without basically melting like Frosty the Snowman.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590942171ra/29572574.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But a girl's gotta do what a girl's gotta do. <br>She makes some new friends! And by <i>makes friends</i>, I mean she kind of forces some of these magical folks that hate humans to help her.<br>Good things happen, bad things happen, and spoilery things happen. <br><b>And then the story is over.</b><br><br>I liked it! Glad I went ahead and finished this trilogy.</span>

    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5409562-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589761149p2/5409562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2210581653?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/5409562-leah">Leah</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5409562-leah?shelf=historical">historical</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5409562-leah?shelf=i-m-not-crying-you-re-crying">i-m-not-crying-you-re-crying</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2210581653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8264082437955016529">1-12-19 So I’ve sung this trilogy’s praises since THE BEAR AND THE NIGHTINGALE and I will continue to declare my love for these books. <br/><br/>Where do I start? I was bawling my eyes out in the first 30 pages and couldn’t stop for a good twenty minutes. The action scenes are engaging. The writing still moves with the dreamy beauty of a fairy tale. We learn more about Vasya’s legacy, which is just as mystical as readers of the series imagined. <br/><br/>And yet I had some minor quibbles. I had some issues with Vas</span>
  <span id="freeText8264082437955016529" style="display:none">1-12-19 So I’ve sung this trilogy’s praises since THE BEAR AND THE NIGHTINGALE and I will continue to declare my love for these books. <br /><br />Where do I start? I was bawling my eyes out in the first 30 pages and couldn’t stop for a good twenty minutes. The action scenes are engaging. The writing still moves with the dreamy beauty of a fairy tale. We learn more about Vasya’s legacy, which is just as mystical as readers of the series imagined. <br /><br />And yet I had some minor quibbles. I had some issues with Vasya this time around. Some of her choices, done on whims, have major consequences that are, for lack of a better word, aggravating. She has grown a lot since, but in this book, she seems more immature compared to when we first met her. The major choices just seemed un-Vasya. And the frost demon is almost a non-entity in the book. Granted, he is a fleeting presence in the first two books, but in here, he vanishes for a major portion of the story. However, the scenes between him and Vasya still have that sparkling chemistry, and there is one moment that had me internally screaming with joy. I have a huge crush on him and that love is never going away. <br /><br />I still love this series and see a lot of possibilities with spin offs (seriously, can we get a book about Morozko, please and thank you), I will treasure the series as it is. <br /><br />________________________<br /><br />5-19-18: The publisher pushed the release date back to 2019... my...precious! :(<br />-----------------------------------------------<br />I want this book like Gollum wants the One Ring.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2193745144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193745144" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193745144?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fan-girl-mode">fan-girl-mode</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=intiguing-concept">intiguing-concept</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=cover-ecstasy">cover-ecstasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=triggers">triggers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=best-young-adult">best-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=dark-haired-heroine">dark-haired-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=messed-me-up">messed-me-up</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193745144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7190263211930278342"><p>
  <i>**Review is posted <a href='https://onethousandandonebook.wordpress.com/2018/12/29/arc-review-the-winter-of-the-witch-winternight-trilogy-3-by-katherine-arden/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> on my blog**</i>
  <br/>
</p><p><b>Real rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><i><b><blockquote>Who is to say, in the end, that the three guardians of Russia are not a witch, a frost-demon, and a chaos-spirit? I find it fitting.<br/>-Katherine Arden, The Winter of the Witch</blockquote></b></i><br/>I am sitting in front of a window, watching snow slowly drifting down from the sky, covering the ground with the carpet of pristine white. Frost and cold. I am thinking about the fairy-tales from faraway memory that, once upon a time, made me shiver with dread a</p></span>
  <span id="freeText7190263211930278342" style="display:none"><p>
  <i>**Review is posted <a href="https://onethousandandonebook.wordpress.com/2018/12/29/arc-review-the-winter-of-the-witch-winternight-trilogy-3-by-katherine-arden/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> on my blog**</i>
  <br />
</p><p><b>Real rating: 4.5 stars</b><br /><i><b><blockquote>Who is to say, in the end, that the three guardians of Russia are not a witch, a frost-demon, and a chaos-spirit? I find it fitting.<br />-Katherine Arden, The Winter of the Witch</blockquote></b></i><br />I am sitting in front of a window, watching snow slowly drifting down from the sky, covering the ground with the carpet of pristine white. Frost and cold. I am thinking about the fairy-tales from faraway memory that, once upon a time, made me shiver with dread and excitement. Such a distant memory, but so warm. This is how my childhood tastes like. <b>Katherine Arden is a sea-witch with an ancient Russian soul.</b> With her enchanting words, she made me long for my childhood fairy-tales. And this is how true magic feels like. <br /> <br />Doubtless, <i>The Winter of the Witch</i> is <b>the most fascinating book of the trilogy</b>. You know why? Because it is filled to the brim with fairy-tale creatures, frost-demons, firebirds and nature. The kind of nature where mysterious magical things happen, the ones you want to be a witness to. And you don't have to be Russian to feel them. You just have to keep your eyes open. <br /><br /><b>So much happens in the span of 400 pages</b>: human cruelty, death, magical adventure, love, treason, war, and, then, peace. And still, it was not enough! I want more of <i>Midnight travels</i>; I want to see faraway lands and realms and times. All is possible in the <i>Winternight</i>. And maybe one day, we'll encounter more of Vasya's travels. I wish...<br /><br /><b>Vasya is the heroine you cannot stop admiring</b>. Such a growth from book 1! She transformed from a barefoot child into a grown fierce woman any creature would be honored to follow. She is brave, she is loyal - she is a true hero everyone needed. <br /><i><blockquote>“I am a witch. I have plucked snowdrops at Midwinter, died at my own choosing, and wept for a nightingale. Now I am beyond prophecy.”</blockquote> </i><br />And <b>Morozko</b>! What a hero! He is not your typical knight in shining armor; he is <b>complex and tormented by his own demons</b> - he <i>is</i> the winter-demon. He is ancient and, at times, he feels distant, but he was there for Vasya, he wanted to be more human because of her. How could my heart not beat faster when Morozko was near? <i>How</i> could I not melt every time Vasya and Morozko were together? It's just beyond my strength to fight these two. <br /><i><blockquote>“Love is for those who know the griefs of time, for it goes hand in hand with loss. An eternity, so burdened, would be a torment. And yet—” He broke off, drew breath. “Yet what else to call it, this terror and this joy?”</blockquote></i><br />I need a frost-demon of my own. I think I'll make it my life goal to find one. Besides, I live in a country where winter lasts up to 5 months, so I might wander in the forest sometime, and look for the hero of my story. <br /><br />Apart from the magic and incredibly reliable characters, can we talk about the historical aspect and cultural accuracy? In all my reviews to the trilogy I seem to be unable to stop praise <i>Katherine Arden</i> for the hard work of researching, more than that - living in the world she has created, because <b>only when you are in something with the whole of your heart, can you create something so beautiful and endearing.</b> To take the old and almost forgotten pagan culture and merge it masterly into the context of the - no less old and controversial - historical events, seamlessly merge the two, thus creating a wonderful story that conquers hearts of thousands of readers all over the world. Pure magic, if you ask me. <br />And if you were wondering, yes, <i>paganism</i> still exists, otherwise, how would I be able to run naked in the rain and make bloody sacrifices occasionally? <br /><br />An amazing journey has come to an end. I am sad. Part of my heart stays with these books and will come back to them over and over again. But for now, <b>can I just ask a <i>Firebird</i> to take me away to faraway lands of witches, frost-demons and chaos-spirits?</b><br /><br /><i>Note: all quotes are taken from the uncorrected ebook copy and are subjected to change in the final version of the book.</i></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="7190263211930278342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2626572131?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" href="/user/show/32340179-jennifer-tarheelreader">Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2626572131" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17272091366150691425"><b>5 stars!</b> <br/><br/><b>I feel like this is a non-review because it was so hard to write and pinpoint the experience of reading this book and series. In short, I absolutely loved it.</b><br/><br/>Wow, this book. If you are a fan of this series, it’s one you just have to jump into; don’t read reviews. Experience every word. Every mesmerizing thought of this masterful author. I’m going to keep my review brief to protect all the fun. In fact, I think this is truly a mini review. <br/><br/>Moscow is in ruins, and Vasya is blamed for ever</span>
  <span id="freeText17272091366150691425" style="display:none"><b>5 stars!</b> <br /><br /><b>I feel like this is a non-review because it was so hard to write and pinpoint the experience of reading this book and series. In short, I absolutely loved it.</b><br /><br />Wow, this book. If you are a fan of this series, it’s one you just have to jump into; don’t read reviews. Experience every word. Every mesmerizing thought of this masterful author. I’m going to keep my review brief to protect all the fun. In fact, I think this is truly a mini review. <br /><br />Moscow is in ruins, and Vasya is blamed for everything by the people around her. They believe her gifts have caused all that has gone wrong. Vasya learns more about who she is and what she can do as she explores her special powers. <br /><br />Medieval Russia in this fantastical world continues to be depicted with its bitter cold. Winter of the Witch is a bold fairytale, and it is lush to the senses. This book has more of a warring focus, and my interest lagged a little during those bits, but the expected magical creatures are present to carry to the fulfilling ending for this amazing trilogy.<br /><br />Kudos to the author for a job exceptionally well-done, and I cannot wait to see what else Katherine Arden has in store for us. Total book love. <br /><br />Thanks to the publishers for the complimentary copy. All opinions are my own. <br /><br />My reviews can also be found on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jennifertarheelreader.com">www.jennifertarheelreader.com</a></span>

<div id="review_2349787245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2349787245" />
    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7383561-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374678939p2/7383561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2349787245?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/7383561-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=fantasy-science-fiction">fantasy-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2349787245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5654553904889919559"><b>I realize it's only January, but I predict this will be one of my favorite books I read this year.</b> This trilogy, what can I say about it without spoiling anything for those who have not read it yet? Well, if you took some Russian history and folklore, some historical misogyny and religious zealotry, a fantastic heroine, two very interesting sets of twins, some romance, some family drama, death, chaos, and redemption - you would get this series. It will be like nothing you have read before (well,</span>
  <span id="freeText5654553904889919559" style="display:none"><b>I realize it's only January, but I predict this will be one of my favorite books I read this year.</b> This trilogy, what can I say about it without spoiling anything for those who have not read it yet? Well, if you took some Russian history and folklore, some historical misogyny and religious zealotry, a fantastic heroine, two very interesting sets of twins, some romance, some family drama, death, chaos, and redemption - you would get this series. It will be like nothing you have read before (well, for us non-Russian readers anyways) and you will (hopefully) love it. I think each book gets even better as this series goes along, so even if you are a little on the fence after book 1, still give book 2 a try. This series is going on my beloved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/7383561?shelf=favorite-series" rel="nofollow noopener">favorite series shelf</a>. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14795541495892133120"><i>
  <b>“I have been running through the dark, trying to save all who have need of me. I have done good and I have done evil, but I am neither. I am only myself.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>The Winter of the Witch starts off directly after the events of The Girl in the Tower. The pace is faster than it’s predecessors but just as mesmerising. If you’ve read my reviews of book 1 and 2, you already know my thoughts on the writing. But just in case you need a reminder: IT. IS. PHENOMENAL.<br/><br/>Magical and mesmerising. I honesty can’t ev</span>
  <span id="freeText14795541495892133120" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“I have been running through the dark, trying to save all who have need of me. I have done good and I have done evil, but I am neither. I am only myself.”</b>
</i><br /><br />The Winter of the Witch starts off directly after the events of The Girl in the Tower. The pace is faster than it’s predecessors but just as mesmerising. If you’ve read my reviews of book 1 and 2, you already know my thoughts on the writing. But just in case you need a reminder: IT. IS. PHENOMENAL.<br /><br />Magical and mesmerising. I honesty can’t even put into words how obsessed I am with her style.<br /><br />So many things happen in this one and Arden really imparted it spectacularly. With everything going on in the plot, it never felt overwhelming.<br /><br />The setting of this one included not just Russia but also a magical midnight land.<br /><br />She just…. She just keeps blowing me away with her creative genius. I cant even deal<br /><br />The character growth was top notch. I didn’t think my admiration for Vasya could grow, but it did. This girl went through SO MUCH during this book alone, she’s truly a hero of the ages.<br /><br />Morozko, Sasha and Marya are as beloved to me as Vasya is.<br /><br />New characters were introduced (I love you Deb Grib 😭❤) and old characters made a comeback. Arden really deserves props for reintroducing old villains in a way that did not feel recycled and lazy.<br /><br />The ending tore me to pieces. I was so distraught, I might have glared at my book for a good 20 minutes before finishing those last few pages.<br /><br />This series is perfection from start to finish. And even though it breaks my heart to say goodbye to these characters, I am already anticipating the next time I’ll pick it up again. I know it will be just as good as the first time Arden’s words drew me into med evil Russia.<br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30036082-warda" rel="nofollow noopener">she who also loves morozko</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2191226261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2191226261" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2191226261?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38391059-the-winter-of-the-witch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2191226261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8580707592378831579">I have so much to say about this book that I’ve been holding back reviewing it until I had time to fully invest myself in my thoughts. I know it’s only March, but I think this is my favourite read of 2019 and it’ll be pretty tough to beat. <br/><br/>In the third book of the Winternight Trilogy we follow Vasya immediately on from the conclusion to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917.The_Girl_in_the_Tower__Winternight_Trilogy___2_' title='The Girl in the Tower (Winternight Trilogy, #2) by Katherine Arden' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl in the Tower</a>. There’s no time to catch your breath, no month long interval, it’s straight into the heart of the action and issues surrounding Vasya and </span>
  <span id="freeText8580707592378831579" style="display:none">I have so much to say about this book that I’ve been holding back reviewing it until I had time to fully invest myself in my thoughts. I know it’s only March, but I think this is my favourite read of 2019 and it’ll be pretty tough to beat. <br /><br />In the third book of the Winternight Trilogy we follow Vasya immediately on from the conclusion to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917.The_Girl_in_the_Tower__Winternight_Trilogy___2_" title="The Girl in the Tower (Winternight Trilogy, #2) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Tower</a>. There’s no time to catch your breath, no month long interval, it’s straight into the heart of the action and issues surrounding Vasya and her family. There are riots and pitchforks, fires, and accusations of witchcraft and sorcery. And leading the rabble is a certain priest with a silvery tongue, guided by an ancient enemy now released from his prison. Arden has such a way with words I fell immediately back into this world, experiencing everything alongside Vasya and Solovey. The confusion, the chaos, the sights and smells of Moscow just jump from the page and I felt their anxiety and fear right there with them. When you’re crying before you’ve even reached 10% in a book, you know it’s touched you deeply. <br /><br />When this writing craftmenship is interwoven so perfectly with magical folklore and real, known, history it combines to make a truly exceptional read. I loved the introduction of the mysterious territory known as ‘Midnight’ and the field of horses. Getting to see some of Solovey’s, and later Vasya’s, mysterious past was bittersweet and touching too, and just added to Vasya’s strength of character. The descriptions of seasons past, as we walk this journey, is wonderfully descriptive and fully immersive again. The plot is always driven and forceful, and the pace continues throughout with multiple twist and battles. <br /><br />Vasya has also come so far as a character, and it was an absolute pleasure to see her develop further here. She’s constantly trying to learn who, or what, she is, while trying not to give in to the free spirit inside her that tells her to flee into winter. She’s willing to sacrifice everything, including her supposedly immortal soul, for her family, and I loved her for that. Her ability to admit her failings, while still yearning to be what she’s expected to be makes her vulnerable yet deeply endearing. She’s a complex woman with strong convictions and a moral backbone that is decidedly unique and wonderful to read. <br /><br />The priest Konstantin is another deliciously complicated character. His mixture of pure hatred and lust for Vasya has not quelled, fuelled by his relationship with a spirit who takes pleasure from suffering and internal torment. He’s a deeply troubled man with a gift for creating beautiful things, and although he hates Vasya he hates himself more. There’s a strange mix of pity and anger that I felt when reading about Konstantin. At some of the truly terrible things he does, I hated him like no other, yet Arden has this ability to make me feel sorry for him. It’s close to how Vasya feels towards him too, and to see both of their internal struggles towards the other is quite electrifying. <br /><br />I couldn’t write this review without touching on Vasya and Morozko’s relationship. At once deeply complicated, and now, rather fractured, we see each of them learn from one another, and what they are to each other. It’s touching and beautiful, sweet and passionate all at once, but never overpowers or is as important to the storyline as Vasya herself is. She never needs Morozko to fulfill her destiny, but rather must discover it for herself and rescue him. It’s a reversal of the stereotypical ‘girl in the tower’ (which makes it even more ironic given the title of the previous book in the series). I love Morozko. His icyness, aloofness, quite literally melts when Vasya gets through his defences. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Solovey. How can I write about what happens to Solovey? Heartbreaking. And it’s never swept under the carpet or used simply as a plot device. The grief is always there, always apparent when Vasya looks at other horses. The guilt and ache she feels when riding the ‘fire bird’ feels so real, and respectful to Solovey’s memory, that I felt deeply touched by it. I haven’t sobbed over a book in a while, but this managed to grab hold of me very tightly and feel that grief personally.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />A really wonderful, magic story full of folklore and history, love and friendship. A must read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8580707592378831579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2592760873?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lily ☁️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lily ☁️" href="/user/show/10148904-lily">lily ☁️</a>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785039720" href="/book/show/38204047-the-winter-of-the-witch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2592760873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13252941438932422198">➳ <b>3 1/2 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“I have plucked snowdrops at Midwinter, died at my own choosing, and wept for a nightingale. Now I am beyond prophecy.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I’ve been pondering over how to review <i>The Winter of the Witch</i> for the longest time, and I simply couldn’t find the right words, or the right way to start. In the end, I decided to go about writing my review in a different way for this book, because it’s … special.<br/><br/>Instead of pointing out the many, many aspects of it that absolutely amazed me (and there were many</span>
  <span id="freeText13252941438932422198" style="display:none">➳ <b>3 1/2 stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“I have plucked snowdrops at Midwinter, died at my own choosing, and wept for a nightingale. Now I am beyond prophecy.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I’ve been pondering over how to review <i>The Winter of the Witch</i> for the longest time, and I simply couldn’t find the right words, or the right way to start. In the end, I decided to go about writing my review in a different way for this book, because it’s … special.<br /><br />Instead of pointing out the many, many aspects of it that absolutely amazed me (and there were many), and the ones that didn’t quite manage to—The Winter of the Witch, for some unknown, quite baffling reason, didn’t entirely touch my heart, in the end—I’m going to list three reasons why you should absolutely read this book.<br /><br />Because despite ending up being a spectator of its beauty from a small distance, rather than reveling in it, I still believe with my entire heart that this is an incredible book that’s part of a book series no one should miss out on.<br /><br /><b>The beautiful writing</b><br /><br />You all know how much I love beautifully written books (I dedicated an entire blog post to books with gorgeous prose after all, so it stands to reason that it’s pretty high on my list of aspects to gush about), and Katherine Arden’s writing is truly arresting in its beauty. I’m usually a fast reader, but I read this book much more slowly than others, simply because I wanted to take my time to appreciate it, and soak in every single word.<br /><br /><b>The setting</b><br /><br />The Winter of the Witch is a Russian inspired fantasy that, for the most part, is set during the wintertime, and I truly felt like I could taste the snow on my lips, feel the tree branches crunch beneath the soles of my shoes, and hear the sound of hooves on the ground, as I accompanied the main character Vasya on her journey.<br /><br />All the surroundings were described with so much care, without going overboard, or distracting from the story itself, and it was truly wondrous to see Moscow come to life before my eyes.<br /><br /><b>The feminist aspect</b><br /><br />The <i>Winternight</i> Trilogy has been delightfully feminist from the very beginning, which I absolutely adore. We can never have too many books featuring fierce, determined, and unapologetic female characters, and The Winter of the Witch only deepened my appreciation for them.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“My fate and my life lie beyond your judgement.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />All in all, <i>The Winter of the Witch</i> was a delight to read, and I can only whole-heartedly recommend everyone to pick up this stunning conclusion to a magical series—it tells a story that will doubtlessly stay with you for many, many years to come.<br /><br /><i>Thank you so much to Del Rey for sending me an ARC of this book! It in no way influenced my opinion, or rating.</i><br /><br />*<br /><br />This book is absolutely gorgeous, and I’m the luckiest girl in the world to have received a proof from the publisher. :’)<br /><br /><blockquote>// <b>buddy read</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">a fave</a> 💖</blockquote><br /><br /><a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/sprinkles-dreams-19449885" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sprinklesofdreamsx/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://sprinklesofdreams.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/sprnklsofdreams" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13252941438932422198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZPZnuGNI5fQ/mXKJKWem2WrwBDsQgMGhUXEA8dzaKNG0PgMr/3+PNpYIBUl0TLap/wJMj9MNWMzTtPx4Bgj1dg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FQHNf+R4mOMqvH16lFalSCAnywszIuAW9fMqRQsYWC/FyanseE/yIYMtCrrJfbU4tdWDv/CveXt3NtbM0cqFiA==')})
  }

But Vasilisa doesn\'t mind—she spends the winter nights huddled around the embers of a fire with her beloved siblings, listening to her nurse\'s fairy tales. Above all, she loves the chilling story of Frost, the blue-eyed winter demon, who appears in the frigid night to claim unwary souls. Wise Russians fear him, her nurse says, and honor the spirits of house and yard and forest that protect their homes from evil.\n\nAfter Vasilisa\'s mother dies, her father goes to Moscow and brings home a new wife. Fiercely devout, city-bred, Vasilisa\'s new stepmother forbids her family from honoring the household spirits. The family acquiesces, but Vasilisa is frightened, sensing that more hinges upon their rituals than anyone knows.\n\nAnd indeed, crops begin to fail, evil creatures of the forest creep nearer, and misfortune stalks the village. All the while, Vasilisa\'s stepmother grows ever harsher in her determination to groom her rebellious stepdaughter for either marriage or confinement in a convent.\n\nAs danger circles, Vasilisa must defy even the people she loves and call on dangerous gifts she has long concealed—this, in order to protect her family from a threat that seems to have stepped from her nurse\'s most frightening
